ORIGINAL REFERENCE: 
Büntgen, U., W. Tegel, K. Nicolussi, M. McCormick, D. Frank, 
V. Trouet, J.O. Kaplan, F. Herzig, K.-U. Heussner, H. Wanner, 
J. Luterbacher, and J. Esper. 2011. 
2500 Years of European Climate Variability and Human Susceptibility. 
Science, Vol. 331, pp. 578-583, 4 February 2011. 
DOI: 10.1126/science.1197175 

ABSTRACT: 
Climate variations influenced the agricultural productivity, 
health risk, and conflict level of preindustrial societies. 
Discrimination between environmental and anthropogenic impacts 
on past civilizations, however, remains difficult because of 
the paucity of high-resolution paleoclimatic evidence. 
We present tree ring-based reconstructions of central European 
summer precipitation and temperature variability over the past 
2500 years. Recent warming is unprecedented, but modern 
hydroclimatic variations may have at times been exceeded 
in magnitude and duration. Wet and warm summers occurred 
during periods of Roman and medieval prosperity. Increased 
climate variability from ~250 to 600 C.E. coincided with 
the demise of the western Roman Empire and the turmoil of 
the Migration Period. Such historical data may provide a basis 
for counteracting the recent political and fiscal reluctance 
to mitigate projected climate change. 



ADDITIONAL REFERENCES: 
Büntgen, U., et al. 2010. 
Tree-ring indicators of German summer drought over the last millennium. 
Quaternary Science Reviews, Vol. 29, pp. 1005-1016.

GEOGRAPHIC REGION: Central Europe 
PERIOD OF RECORD: 500 BC - 2008 AD

DESCRIPTION:  
Tree ring-based reconstructions of central European summer 
precipitation and temperature over the past 2500 years.
Precipitation is reconstructed for April-May-June, 
and temperature anomalies for June-July-August.  



DATA: 
1. Reconstructed AMJ precipitation totals and JJA temperature anomalies. 
(Data corresponding to Fig. 4).  Error bars are RMSE of the calibration 
periods (1901-1980 for precipitation and 1864-2003 for temperature).
Independent precipitation and temperature reconstructions from Germany
(Büntgen et al. 2010 QSR) and the Swiss Alps (Büntgen et al. 2006 JClim)
also included for comparison. 

Column 1: Year AD 
Column 2: Reconstructed April-May-June Precipitation (Büntgen et al. 2011 Science)  
Column 3: Reconstructed April-May-June Precipitation -RMSE (Büntgen et al. 2011 Science) 
Column 4: Reconstructed April-May-June Precipitation +RMSE (Büntgen et al. 2011 Science) 
Column 5: Reconstructed Precipitation (Büntgen et al. 2010 QSR)
Column 6: Reconstructed June-July-August Temperature Anomaly (Büntgen et al. 2011 Science)  
Column 7: Reconstructed June-July-August Temperature Anomaly -RMSE (Büntgen et al. 2011 Science) 
Column 8: Reconstructed June-July-August Temperature Anomaly +RMSE  (Büntgen et al. 2011 Science) 
Column 9: Reconstructed Temperature (Büntgen et al. 2006 J.Clim.)
